The Third Proof: Why God's Attribute of Creating Must Be Eternal
A proof that the attribute of creating (khaliqiyya) must be eternal, otherwise absurd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third proof from Al-Matalib al-Aliyah demonstrating that the attribute of creating (khaliqiyya) must be eternal, otherwise absurd consequences follow.

Core Idea
If God's being creator were temporal, it would either need another creator or none at all—both impossible.

In this passage, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi presents the third proof against the temporal origination of the world. The argument focuses on the distinction between God's power (qudra) and His creativity (khaliqiyya). By examining what it means for the world to occur at a specific time, al-Razi shows that assuming the attribute of creation is temporal leads to infinite regress or denial of a creator. This lesson unpacks that reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dilemma
Read the initial two possibilities for why the world occurs at a specific time: either because God is powerful or because He created it at that time. See how the first is rejected.
Notice that the first possibility would require the world to be eternal, which contradicts temporality.
2
Trace the distinction argument
Follow how accepting the second possibility forces a distinction between the concepts of power and creativity. Also see why creativity must be distinct from the created world.
This distinction is crucial for the next step.
3
See the two impossible outcomes
Understand the two reasons why a temporal creative attribute is impossible: it leads to either infinite regress or negation of a creator.
Also note the second reason: a temporal attribute would make God's essence a locus for temporal events.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة : لو كان العالم حادثاً ، لكان حدوثه في الوقت المعين ، إما أن يكون لمجرد كونه قادراً ، أو ليس كذلك . بل لأجل أن الله تعالى أوجده في ذلك الوقت . والأول باطل . لأنه تعالى كان قادراً قبل حصول هذا الوقت ، فكان يجب أن يحدث هذا الحادث قبل حدوث هذا الوقت . بل كان يجب أن يدوم الأثر بدوام كونه قادراً وكما أن قادريته أزلية، لزم أن يكون هذا الأثر أزلياً . وهو المطلوب. وأما القسم الثاني : وهو أن يقال : العالم إنما حدث في هذا الوقت ، لا لأجل أن الله تعالى قادر ، بل لأجل أنه تعالى خلقه في هذا الوقت المعين . فنقول : صدق هذا النفي والإثبات ، يوجب التغاير لا محالة ، فوجب أن يكون المفهوم من كونه تعالى خالقاً للعالم في هذا الوقت المعين مغايرا للفهوم من كونه تعالى قادراً. وإلا لصار مورد النفي والإثبات، أمراً واحداً. وذلك محال. وأيضاً: يجب أن يكون المفهوم من كونه تعالى خالقاً للعالم، مغايراً لنفس العالم . وذلك لأن سبب وجود العالم هو خالقيـة الله تعالى له ، والمؤثر مغاير للأثر . فيثبت : أن المفهوم من الخالقية أمر مغاير للقادرية ، وأمر مغاير لذات المخلوق . وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : لما كان العالم إنما حدث في هذا الوقت لا قبله ولا بعده ، وجب أن يقال : إن كونه تعالى خالقاً له ، إنما حصل في هذا الوقت لا قبله ولا بعده ، لأن قبل حدوث العالم كان العالم باقيا على عـدمـه الأصلي ومتى كان الأثر باقياً على عدمه الأصلي امتنع أن يصدق على المؤثر كونه مؤثراً فيه . فيثبت : أنه لو كان العالم حادثاً ، لكان كونه تعالى خالقاً للعالم صفة حادثة في ذات الله تعالى . فنقول : وهذا محال لوجهين : الأول : إن الحادث إما أن يكون مفتقراً إلى المقتضى ، أو لا يكون كذلك. فإن كان الأول لزم افتقار تلك الخالقية الحادثة إلى خالقية أخرى ولزم التسلسل . وإن كان الثاني وهو أن لا يفتقر الحادث إلى الخالق ، فحينئذ يستغني حدوث العالم في ذلك الوقت عن الخالق ، وذلك يقتضي نفي الخالق . فيثبت : أن القول بحدوث العالم ، يوجب نفي المؤثر ونفي الخالق ، وذلك محال . فما أدى إليه كان محالاً. الثاني : إن حدوث الصفة في ذات الله تعالى ، يقتضي كون ذاته محلاً للحوادث ، وأنه محال . على ما بيناه بالبراهين القاطعة ، فكان هذا القول باطلاً . والله أعلم
The third proof: If the world were temporal, then its occurrence at a specific time would either be due to its mere being powerful (qādir), or not so; rather because God created it at that time. The first is false because He was powerful before the arrival of this time; so this event should have occurred before the occurrence of this time; rather the effect should be perpetual by the perpetuity of His being powerful; and just as His power (qādiriyya) is eternal, this effect would necessarily be eternal. That is what is sought. As for the second division: that it is said: The world occurred at this time, not because God is powerful, but because He created it at this specific time. So we say: The truth of this negation and affirmation necessarily entails distinction (taghāyur); so it is necessary that the concept of His being creator (khāliq) of the world at this specific time be distinct from the concept of His being powerful (qādir). Otherwise the object of negation and affirmation would become one thing, and that is impossible. Also, it is necessary that the concept of His being creator of the world be distinct from the world itself; because the cause of the world's existence is God's creativity (khāliqiyya) for it, and the cause (mu'aththir) is distinct from the effect. So it is established that the concept of creativity is something distinct from power (qādiriyya) and distinct from the essence of the created. And when this is established, we say: Since the world only occurred at this time, not before it and not after it, it must be said that His being creator of it only came to be at this time, not before it and not after it; because before the occurrence of the world, the world remained in its original non-existence, and whenever the effect remains in its original non-existence, it is impossible to truthfully predicate of the cause that it is a cause with respect to it. So it is established: If the world were temporal, then His being creator of the world would be a temporal attribute in the essence of God. We say: And this is impossible for two reasons: The first: The temporal event either stands in need of a requirer (muqtaḍā) or not. If the first, then that temporal creativity would need another creativity, leading to an infinite regress (tasalsul). If the second, i.e., the temporal event does not need a creator, then the occurrence of the world at that time would be independent of the creator, which entails the negation of the creator. So it is established that the statement of the world's temporality entails the negation of the cause and the negation of the creator, and that is impossible. So whatever leads to it is impossible. The second: The occurrence of an attribute in the essence of God requires His essence to be a locus for temporal events (maḥall li-l-ḥawādith), and that is impossible, as we have demonstrated with decisive proofs. So this statement is false. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is the third proof (al-ḥujja al-thālitha) arguing against the temporal origination of the world (ḥudūth al-‘ālam). The proof is structured as follows: It first presents a dilemma: if the world were temporal (ḥādith), its occurrence at a specific time must have a reason. Two possibilities are considered: (1) It occurred simply because God is powerful (qādir). (2) It occurred because God brought it into existence at that time. The first possibility is rejected: since God's power is eternal and unchanging, if the mere fact of being powerful sufficed, the world would have existed eternally—contradicting its temporality. Thus the second possibility must be examined. The argument then shows that accepting the second possibility forces a distinction (taghāyur) between the concepts of 'being powerful' (qādiriyya) and 'being creator' (khāliqiyya). Moreover, 'being creator' must also be distinct from the created world itself, because the cause is distinct from the effect. Given that the world came into existence at a specific time, the attribute of 'being creator' (khāliqiyya) would have to arise at that moment—meaning it is a temporal attribute in God. This is then shown to be impossible for two reasons (wajhayn): (i) If the temporal attribute is created, it would require another creator, leading to infinite regress (tasalsul). If it is not created, then the world's occurrence at that time would have no need for a creator, negating the very concept of a creator. (ii) A temporal attribute in God would make His essence a locus for temporal events (maḥall li-l-ḥawādith), which is impossible for God. Thus, the assumption of the world's temporality leads to absurdities, proving that the world must be eternal.

Key Terms
قادر (powerful)
قادرية (power)
خالق (creator)
خالقية (creativity)
التغاير (distinction)
حادث (temporal event)
التسلسل (infinite regress)
محلاً للحوادث (locus of temporal events)
مقتضى (requirer)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the argument denies that God creates in time; it actually argues that the attribute of being creator is eternal, not that the act of creation is eternal.
Correction: The proof aims to show that khāliqiyya is an eternal attribute; the temporal act of creation does not imply a temporal attribute. The argument is about the attribute, not the act.

Checkpoint
According to the third proof, why is it impossible for God's attribute of being creator (خالقية) to be temporal?
A) Because it would imply that God's power is not eternal.
B) Because it would lead to either infinite regress or the negation of a creator.
C) Because the concept of creator is the same as the concept of powerful.
D) Because the world must be temporal.

Key Takeaway
The attribute of creating (khāliqiyya) must be eternal; its temporality leads to either infinite regress or denial of God's role as creator, both of which are impossible for God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God's attribute of creating is eternal, meaning that your very existence at every moment depends on His eternal creative power? If so, why do you still feel self-sufficient in your daily decisions and achievements? Let this proof shatter the illusion of independence and drive you to rely on Him completely.
?
The argument shows that if God's creatorship were temporal, it would either need another creator or no creator at all—both impossible. Is there any area of your life where you act as if God's role is optional? Where you feel you can manage without His constant creative support? Identify one such area today and bring it before Him in prayer, acknowledging that you are nothing without His eternal act of creation.
?
The proof emphasizes that God cannot be a locus of change. Yet, how often do you treat God as if He is affected by your actions—angry when you sin, pleased when you obey—as if His essence changes? This proof calls you to worship a God who is unchangingly perfect, beyond temporal emotions. How will you adjust your worship and trust in light of His immutability?

Two Absurdities of a Temporal Creator Attribute
Sanusi argues against temporal creatorship with two absurdities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi argues that God's attribute of being creator cannot be temporal, and the two absurd consequences that follow from such a claim.

Core Idea
If God's creatorship were temporal, it would lead to either infinite regress or denying the Creator altogether.

Sanusi presents a sophisticated logical argument against the idea that God's attribute of being creator is temporal. He first establishes that creatorship is distinct from omnipotence and from the world itself. Then he shows that if the world is temporal, God's creatorship would also be temporal, leading to two impossible consequences. This passage reinforces the Islamic doctrine that God's attributes are eternal and not subject to temporal change.

Guided Path
1
Understand the premise of distinction
Sanusi begins by arguing that the concept of God's creatorship must be distinct from both His omnipotence and the world itself. Grasp this grounding step carefully.
This distinction is crucial for the later argument.
2
Apply the reasoning to a temporal world
Notice how Sanusi deduces that if the world began at a specific time, then God's attribute of creating that world must also have begun at that time.
3
Examine the first absurdity
The temporal attribute would either require another creatorship (infinite regress) or be independent of a creator (denial of God). Both are impossible.
This is a classic argument against temporal attributes.
4
Examine the second absurdity
A temporal attribute would make God's essence a locus for temporal events, which is impossible for God.
Sanusi refers to prior proofs against this.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The overall conclusion is that the claim of a temporal world leads to impossible consequences, so it must be false.
This is an indirect proof (burhan al-‘aksi) of God's eternity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فنقول : صدق هذا النفي والإثبات يوجب التغاير لا محالة، فوجب أن يكون المفهوم من كونه تعالى خالقاً للعالم في هذا الوقت المعين مغايراً للمفهوم من كونه تعالى قادراً. وإلا لصار مورد النفي والإثبات أمراً واحداً. وذلك محال. وأيضاً: يجب أن يكون المفهوم من كونه تعالى خالقاً للعالم مغايراً لنفس العالم. وذلك لأن سبب وجود العالم هو خالقية الله تعالى له، والمؤثر مغاير للأثر. فيثبت أن المفهوم من الخالقية أمر مغاير للقادرية وأمر مغاير لذات المخلوق. وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : لما كان العالم إنما حدث في هذا الوقت لا قبله ولا بعده، وجب أن يقال إن كونه تعالى خالقاً له إنما حصل في هذا الوقت لا قبله ولا بعده، لأن قبل حدوث العالم كان العالم باقياً على عدمه الأصلي، ومتى كان الأثر باقياً على عدمه الأصلي امتنع أن يصدق على المؤثر كونه مؤثراً فيه. فيثبت أنه لو كان العالم حادثاً لكان كونه تعالى خالقاً للعالم صفة حادثة في ذات الله تعالى. فنقول: وهذا محال لوجهين: الأول: إن الحادث إما أن يكون مفتقراً إلى المقتضى أو لا يكون كذلك. فإن كان الأول لزم افتقار تلك الخالقية الحادثة إلى خالقية أخرى ولزم التسلسل. وإن كان الثاني وهو أن لا يفتقر الحادث إلى الخالق فحينئذ يستغني حدوث العالم في ذلك الوقت عن الخالق وذلك يقتضي نفي الخالق. فيثبت أن القول بحدوث العالم يوجب نفي المؤثر ونفي الخالق وذلك محال. فما أدى إليه كان محالاً. الثاني: إن حدوث الصفة في ذات الله تعالى يقتضي كون ذاته محلاً للحوادث وأنه محال على ما بيناه بالبراهين القاطعة، فكان هذا القول باطلاً.
We say: The truth of this negation and affirmation necessarily entails distinction. So it is necessary that the concept of His being—Exalted is He—a creator of the world at this specific time is distinct from the concept of His being—Exalted is He—omnipotent. Otherwise, the subject of negation and affirmation would be one thing. That is impossible. Also: It is necessary that the concept of His being—Exalted is He—a creator of the world is distinct from the world itself. That is because the cause of the world's existence is God's being its creator, and the cause is distinct from the effect. So it is established that the concept of creatorship is distinct from the concept of omnipotence and distinct from the essence of the creature. When this is established, we say: Since the world only occurred at this time, not before or after, it must be said that His being—Exalted is He—its creator only occurred at this time, not before or after, because before the world's occurrence the world was remaining in its original non-existence, and when the effect remains in its original non-existence it is impossible that the cause is truthfully described as having effectiveness in it. So it is established that if the world were temporal, then His being—Exalted is He—a creator of the world would be a temporal attribute in God's essence. We say: This is impossible for two reasons: First: The temporal is either dependent on a necessitation or not. If the first, then that temporal creatorship would be dependent on another creatorship, leading to infinite regress. If the second—that the temporal is not dependent on the Creator—then the world's occurrence at that time would be independent of the Creator, and that entails the denial of the Creator. So it is established that the statement that the world is temporal entails the denial of the cause and the denial of the Creator, and that is impossible. So what leads to it is impossible. Second: The occurrence of an attribute in God's essence entails that His essence is a locus for temporal events, and that is impossible, as we have demonstrated with conclusive proofs. So this statement is false.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of an argument against the claim that the world is temporal (حادث). It begins by establishing that the concept of God being a creator is distinct from both His attribute of being powerful (قادرية) and from the world itself. Then it applies this to the temporal occurrence of the world: if the world began at a specific time, then God's attribute of creating that world must also have occurred at that time. This would make God's attribute of creatorship temporal. The passage then presents two reasons why a temporal attribute in God is impossible. First, if the temporal attribute (the creatorship) is dependent on a cause, it would require another creatorship, leading to infinite regress (تسلسل). If it is not dependent on a cause, then the world's occurrence would not need a creator at all, effectively denying God. Both alternatives are absurd. The second reason is that a temporal attribute in God would make His essence a locus for temporal events (محل للحوادث), which is impossible for God, as established by prior conclusive proofs. The argument follows a logical structure: it first establishes the distinction of concepts, then deduces the temporality of the attribute, then refutes it with two absurdities.

القادرية
التغاير
الحادث
المقتضى
التسلسل
محل للحوادث

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's attributes can be temporal without affecting His essence.
Correction: Sanusi shows that a temporal attribute necessarily makes the essence a locus for temporal events, which is impossible for God.

Checkpoint

A) It would make God a locus for temporal events.
B) It would lead to either infinite regress or denial of the Creator.
C) It would make the world eternal.
D) It would contradict God's omnipotence.

Key Takeaway
God's attribute of creatorship is eternal, and claiming it is temporal leads to either infinite regress or the denial of a creator, both of which are absurd.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Necessity of God's Eternal Activity
Razi proves God's eternal activity by analyzing the impossibility of change in the First Agent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi proves that God must have been eternally active, as any change in His state would require a change not from Him, which is impossible since all changes are created by Him.

Core Idea
God must be eternally active because inactivity would require a change He could not cause.

This passage presents a rational proof (istidlal) that God's attribute of being an Agent (فاعل) is eternal. The argument begins by considering a hypothetical: if a change in God's action were due to an external circumstance, that circumstance would itself require explanation, leading to an infinite regress. The only alternative—that the change is not from the agent—is valid for created agents but impossible for the First Agent, for He is the source of all change.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the logical flow from conditional to examples to conclusion.
The key terms are فاعل (agent), تغير (change), أزل (eternity), لا يزال (perpetuity).
2
Identify the logical steps
Break down the argument: (1) If change from external, regress; (2) If change not from agent, then examples; (3) But God is First Agent, all changes from Him; (4) Therefore He cannot change from inactive to active; (5) So He must have always been active.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider why this argument eliminates the possibility that God began acting at a point in time. How does it differ from human agents?
Human agents become active due to external changes, but God cannot have external causes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قبله، إذ لو كان من قبله لعاد السؤال الأول (۱) ] فيه . وهو أنه لم غيره في هذا الوقت دون ما قبله وما بعده ؟ وأما إذا كان [ ذلك (٢) ] التغير ليس من قبله ، صح ذلك . مثل : [ أنه (۳) ] لما انتهى النهار إلى آخره ، قام الرجل من مكانه ، وذهب إلى الدار ، ولما قرب هجوم الشتاء أقدم الرجل على تحصيل مهمات الشتاء ، فيثبت بما ذكرنا : أن كل ما كان غير فاعل لم يزل ، فإنه يصير فاعلاً إلا لتغير حصل ، لا من قبله . وهذا في حق الفاعل الأول محال . لأن جميع التغيرات إنما حصل بتكوينه وإيجاده، فإمتنع أن يكون تغيره من ترك الفعل إلى تحصيل الفعل ، لأجل تغير وقع لا من جهته ، فلو كان غير فاعل في الأزل ، وجب أن لا يصير فاعلاً في لا يزال [ وحيث صار فاعلاً في لا يزال (٤) ] علمنا : أنه كان أيضاً فاعلاً في الأزل ، ولا يقال : الغرض من الإيجاد : إيصال النفع إلى الخلق ، لأن هذا الغرض كان مطلوباً قبل ذلك فلم لم يشرع في الفعل ، قبل ذلك ؟ ولا يقال : ذلك الوقت إنما اختص بالإحداث ، لأنه أصلح للمكلفين ، أو لأنه تعين بسبب الإرادة (٥) لأنا نقول : ذلك الوقت الذي هو أصلح لإحداث العالم من سائر الأوقات ، إما أن يحدث بإحداث الله [ تعالى (٦) ] أو لا بإحداثه فإن حدث بإحداث الله تعالى ، عــاد السؤال في أنه : لم فعله ، ولم يفعل غيره ؟ وإن كان لا بإحداث الله تعالى ، فهذا قول بأنه قبل إحداث الله [ تعالى (٧) ] العالم ، كانت الأوقات موجودة ، والتغيرات حاصلة ، فيصير إحداث الله العالم في ذلك الوقت ، جارياً مجرى ما إذا قصد الواحد منا ، إلى السفر حال اعتدال الحر والبرد ، فإنه كان الداعي [ له (۸) ] إلى تحصيل الربح موجوداً قبل ذلك ، إلا أنه كان ينتظر حضور الوقت الموافق لهذا العمل . فلما حضر الوقت الموافق ، أقدم ذلك الفاعل على ذلك العمل . فهذا يقتضي أن تكون الأوقات والتغيرات حاصلة ، لا بإحداث الفاعل الأول . وذلك محال . وتمام الكلام في إبطال هذه السؤالات : قد تقدم ، ولا فائدة في الإعادة . وههنا آخر الوجوه المستنبطة من كونه تعالى فاعلاً ومـوجـداً ، وبالله التوفيق
Before it, because if it were from before it, the first question would return concerning it. That is: why did He do other than this in this time, not before it and not after it? And if that change is not from him, that is valid. For example: when the day ends, the man stands from his place and goes to the house; and when the onset of winter approaches, the man undertakes to procure winter essentials. So it is established by what we mentioned: that everything that was not an agent forever becomes an agent only due to a change that occurred, not from itself. And this is impossible with respect to the First Agent. Because all changes only occur by His creation and bringing into existence, so it is impossible that His change from abandoning action to performing action be due to a change occurring not from His side. So if He was not an agent in eternity, it would be necessary that He would never become an agent in perpetuity. And since He has become an agent in perpetuity, we know that He was also an agent in eternity. And it cannot be said: the purpose of bringing into existence is to convey benefit to creation, because this purpose was desired before that, so why did He not begin the action before that? And it cannot be said: that time was specifically chosen for creation because it was more suitable for the morally responsible, or because it was determined by the will. For we say: that time which is more suitable for the creation of the world than other times, either it arises by God's creation or not by His creation. If it arises by God's creation, the question returns: why did He do it and not do something else? And if it is not by God's creation, then this is a statement that before God's creation of the world, times existed and changes occurred, so God's creation of the world at that time becomes like when one of us intends to travel at a time of moderate temperature, for the motive for him to obtain profit existed before that, but he was waiting for the suitable time for this work. When the suitable time came, that agent undertook that work. This necessitates that times and changes exist not by the creation of the First Agent, and that is impossible. The complete discussion in refuting these objections has preceded, and there is no benefit in repetition. And here ends the points derived from His being an Agent and Creator, and with God is success.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof (istidlal) that God must have been eternally active, followed by refutation of two objections. The argument proceeds in stages:

First, the author considers a hypothetical: if the change that led to God's action were from something other than God (i.e., an external circumstance), then the questioner would ask why that circumstance occurred at that specific time—leading to an infinite regress. But if the change is not from the agent (i.e., it is from God Himself), then the analogy of human actions (e.g., standing when day ends, preparing for winter) shows that a change must occur for an agent to become active. However, this analogy fails for the First Agent because all changes are created by Him. It is impossible that His change from inactivity to activity be due to a change outside His control.

Second, if God were inactive in eternity, He could never become active later because any later change would have to be created by Him—but if He was not yet an agent, that change could not be produced. So the fact that He is now active proves He was always active.

Then the author refutes two objections:
Objection 1: The purpose of creation is to benefit creatures, and that purpose existed before creation, so why delay? Answer: This objection is rejected because it assumes God's action is motivated by external purposes, which is not the case in kalam. The argument does not elaborate further, but points to earlier discussions.
Objection 2: The specific time for creation was chosen because it was most suitable (i.e., optimal for moral responsibility) or determined by God's will. The author dissolves this by a dilemma: if the suitability of that time is also created by God, then the question 'why that time?' simply repeats. If the suitability is not created by God, then independent times and changes exist alongside God, which is impossible (since all times and changes are from Him). The example of a traveler waiting for moderate weather illustrates the latter absurdity: it implies that the world's creation was dependent on pre-existing conditions, making God not the sole originator.

Finally, the author notes that the complete refutation has already been given, and this is the last point derived from God's attribute of being Agent and Creator.

Key Terms
فاعل
تغير
أزل
لا يزال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God was inactive in eternity and then began to act at a later time.
Correction: This is impossible because any change in God would require a cause external to Him, but all changes are created by Him, so He cannot undergo change.

Checkpoint
According to the argument, why is it impossible for God to have been inactive in eternity and then become active?
A) Because all changes are created by God, so His transition from inactivity to activity would require a change not from Him.
B) Because God's will is eternal and cannot change.
C) Because the world is eternal and did not begin in time.
D) Because the purpose of creation benefits creatures, which existed eternally.

Key Takeaway
God's eternal activity is a necessary consequence of His being the sole originator of all change; He cannot change from inactive to active.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God is eternally active, then every breath you take is a direct, ongoing creation from Him. Do you live with the constant awareness that your existence is being recreated each moment, or have you become desensitized to this reality? What would change in your day if you truly felt that?
?
Razi's proof shows that God cannot become inactive. How does this truth confront your trust in Him? In what areas of your life do you act as if God's care is sporadic rather than continuous? Repent of the moments you have doubted His unceasing involvement.
?
The argument forces you to acknowledge that all changes in your life — successes, failures, joys, trials — come from the First Agent alone. Are you attributing the outcomes of your life to secondary causes (people, luck, effort) while forgetting that they are merely instruments? Ask God to realign your heart to see His hand in everything.

Refuting Objections to the Timing of Creation
Razi refutes two objections about the timing of creation using a dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi refutes two objections that attempt to explain why God created the world at a specific time rather than earlier, showing that such explanations either lead to infinite regress or imply pre-existing conditions independent of God.

Core Idea
God's creative act is not conditioned by external purposes or optimal times.

After establishing God's eternal activity, Razi addresses two objections that might arise. The first suggests that God delayed creation to benefit creatures, implying a purpose that existed before creation. The second claims that a specific time was chosen because it was most suitable for moral responsibility or determined by God's will. Razi refutes both by showing that if the suitability is created by God, the question repeats; if not, it implies that times and changes exist without God's creation, which is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the two objections
Read the Arabic and translation for the two objections. Notice how they both try to provide a reason for the timing of creation.
The first objection appeals to benefit, the second to suitability or will.
2
Understand the dilemma response
Focus on the response starting with 'For we say: that time...' It presents a dilemma: either the suitability is created by God or not. Work through each branch.
If created by God, we ask why that time, repeating the question. If not created by God, then times exist independent of God, which is impossible.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this refutation reinforces God's absolute sovereignty. How does it prevent any external condition from determining God's action?
Compare with the human example of a traveler waiting for moderate weather.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قبله، إذ لو كان من قبله لعاد السؤال الأول (۱) ] فيه . وهو أنه لم غيره في هذا الوقت دون ما قبله وما بعده ؟ وأما إذا كان [ ذلك (٢) ] التغير ليس من قبله ، صح ذلك . مثل : [ أنه (۳) ] لما انتهى النهار إلى آخره ، قام الرجل من مكانه ، وذهب إلى الدار ، ولما قرب هجوم الشتاء أقدم الرجل على تحصيل مهمات الشتاء ، فيثبت بما ذكرنا : أن كل ما كان غير فاعل لم يزل ، فإنه يصير فاعلاً إلا لتغير حصل ، لا من قبله . وهذا في حق الفاعل الأول محال . لأن جميع التغيرات إنما حصل بتكوينه وإيجاده، فإمتنع أن يكون تغيره من ترك الفعل إلى تحصيل الفعل ، لأجل تغير وقع لا من جهته ، فلو كان غير فاعل في الأزل ، وجب أن لا يصير فاعلاً في لا يزال [ وحيث صار فاعلاً في لا يزال (٤) ] علمنا : أنه كان أيضاً فاعلاً في الأزل ، ولا يقال : الغرض من الإيجاد : إيصال النفع إلى الخلق ، لأن هذا الغرض كان مطلوباً قبل ذلك فلم لم يشرع في الفعل ، قبل ذلك ؟ ولا يقال : ذلك الوقت إنما اختص بالإحداث ، لأنه أصلح للمكلفين ، أو لأنه تعين بسبب الإرادة (٥) لأنا نقول : ذلك الوقت الذي هو أصلح لإحداث العالم من سائر الأوقات ، إما أن يحدث بإحداث الله [ تعالى (٦) ] أو لا بإحداثه فإن حدث بإحداث الله تعالى ، عــاد السؤال في أنه : لم فعله ، ولم يفعل غيره ؟ وإن كان لا بإحداث الله تعالى ، فهذا قول بأنه قبل إحداث الله [ تعالى (٧) ] العالم ، كانت الأوقات موجودة ، والتغيرات حاصلة ، فيصير إحداث الله العالم في ذلك الوقت ، جارياً مجرى ما إذا قصد الواحد منا ، إلى السفر حال اعتدال الحر والبرد ، فإنه كان الداعي [ له (۸) ] إلى تحصيل الربح موجوداً قبل ذلك ، إلا أنه كان ينتظر حضور الوقت الموافق لهذا العمل . فلما حضر الوقت الموافق ، أقدم ذلك الفاعل على ذلك العمل . فهذا يقتضي أن تكون الأوقات والتغيرات حاصلة ، لا بإحداث الفاعل الأول . وذلك محال . وتمام الكلام في إبطال هذه السؤالات : قد تقدم ، ولا فائدة في الإعادة . وههنا آخر الوجوه المستنبطة من كونه تعالى فاعلاً ومـوجـداً ، وبالله التوفيق
Before it, because if it were from before it, the first question would return concerning it. That is: why did He do other than this in this time, not before it and not after it? And if that change is not from him, that is valid. For example: when the day ends, the man stands from his place and goes to the house; and when the onset of winter approaches, the man undertakes to procure winter essentials. So it is established by what we mentioned: that everything that was not an agent forever becomes an agent only due to a change that occurred, not from itself. And this is impossible with respect to the First Agent. Because all changes only occur by His creation and bringing into existence, so it is impossible that His change from abandoning action to performing action be due to a change occurring not from His side. So if He was not an agent in eternity, it would be necessary that He would never become an agent in perpetuity. And since He has become an agent in perpetuity, we know that He was also an agent in eternity. And it cannot be said: the purpose of bringing into existence is to convey benefit to creation, because this purpose was desired before that, so why did He not begin the action before that? And it cannot be said: that time was specifically chosen for creation because it was more suitable for the morally responsible, or because it was determined by the will. For we say: that time which is more suitable for the creation of the world than other times, either it arises by God's creation or not by His creation. If it arises by God's creation, the question returns: why did He do it and not do something else? And if it is not by God's creation, then this is a statement that before God's creation of the world, times existed and changes occurred, so God's creation of the world at that time becomes like when one of us intends to travel at a time of moderate temperature, for the motive for him to obtain profit existed before that, but he was waiting for the suitable time for this work. When the suitable time came, that agent undertook that work. This necessitates that times and changes exist not by the creation of the First Agent, and that is impossible. The complete discussion in refuting these objections has preceded, and there is no benefit in repetition. And here ends the points derived from His being an Agent and Creator, and with God is success.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof (istidlal) that God must have been eternally active, followed by refutation of two objections. The argument proceeds in stages:

First, the author considers a hypothetical: if the change that led to God's action were from something other than God (i.e., an external circumstance), then the questioner would ask why that circumstance occurred at that specific time—leading to an infinite regress. But if the change is not from the agent (i.e., it is from God Himself), then the analogy of human actions (e.g., standing when day ends, preparing for winter) shows that a change must occur for an agent to become active. However, this analogy fails for the First Agent because all changes are created by Him. It is impossible that His change from inactivity to activity be due to a change outside His control.

Second, if God were inactive in eternity, He could never become active later because any later change would have to be created by Him—but if He was not yet an agent, that change could not be produced. So the fact that He is now active proves He was always active.

Then the author refutes two objections:
Objection 1: The purpose of creation is to benefit creatures, and that purpose existed before creation, so why delay? Answer: This objection is rejected because it assumes God's action is motivated by external purposes, which is not the case in kalam. The argument does not elaborate further, but points to earlier discussions.
Objection 2: The specific time for creation was chosen because it was most suitable (i.e., optimal for moral responsibility) or determined by God's will. The author dissolves this by a dilemma: if the suitability of that time is also created by God, then the question 'why that time?' simply repeats. If the suitability is not created by God, then independent times and changes exist alongside God, which is impossible (since all times and changes are from Him). The example of a traveler waiting for moderate weather illustrates the latter absurdity: it implies that the world's creation was dependent on pre-existing conditions, making God not the sole originator.

Finally, the author notes that the complete refutation has already been given, and this is the last point derived from God's attribute of being Agent and Creator.

إرادة
أصلح
مكلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God delayed creation because He was waiting for the right time or conditions to exist.
Correction: This implies that time exists independently of God and that He is subject to external conditions. In reality, God creates all times and changes, and His action is not conditioned by them.

Checkpoint
According to the dilemma response, what happens if the optimal time for creation is not created by God?
A) It proves that God's will determined the time.
B) It implies that times and changes existed before God's creation, which is impossible.
C) It shows that God's purpose was to benefit creatures.
D) It leads to the same question about why that time was chosen.

Key Takeaway
God's creation is not conditioned by any external factor; the timing of creation is solely by His will, and any attempt to explain it by external causes fails.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself postponing obedience to God until the 'right moment'—a moment that feels more suitable or less difficult? How does this lesson challenge that hidden assumption that you need ideal conditions to act?
?
Think of an area of your life where you have been waiting for circumstances to improve before you submit fully to God. What would it mean for you to act now, without waiting for a 'better time'? Are you trusting in God's command or in the suitability of the timing?
?
If you truly believed that God's will alone determines the right time for everything, how would that change your anxiety about the future and your impatience with the present? What is one specific decision you have delayed that you can take today, without waiting for external conditions?

The Final Refutation: Time and Change Cannot Exist Without God
Final argument against independent times and changes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that time and change cannot exist independently of God's direct causation, and why this is impossible.

Core Idea
Nothing in time or change occurs without God directly causing it.

This lesson presents a final, concise refutation of the objection that times and changes could happen without being initiated by God. The author shows that if an agent only acts at a 'compatible' time, that time itself would be uncaused by God—which is impossible. This argument seals the conclusion that every temporal change is directly from God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and its translation. Notice the concise style and the logical flow: an objection, its implication, and the judgment of impossibility.
The passage references earlier discussion; focus on the core argument here.
2
Understand the 'compatible time' objection
The objection imagines that an agent acts only when a time is 'compatible' (al-muwāfiq) for its action. This suggests that the time itself is not caused by the agent. Identify why the author says this leads to an impossible conclusion.
3
Grasp the impossibility conclusion
If times and changes were to exist without the initiation of the First Agent (God), that would contradict tawḥīd (the oneness of God as Creator). The author states this is impossible (muḥāl). Reflect on why this is a necessary belief in Islamic theology.
The author also notes that the complete discussion has already been given; this is the final summary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الموافق لهذا العمل . فلما حضر الوقت الموافق ، أقدم ذلك الفاعل على ذلك العمل . فهذا يقتضي أن تكون الأوقات والتغيرات حاصلة ، لا بإحداث الفاعل الأول . وذلك محال . وتمام الكلام في إبطال هذه السؤالات : قد تقدم ، ولا فائدة في الإعادة .

The compatible for this action. Then when the compatible time came, that agent undertook that action. This entails that times and changes exist without the initiation of the First Agent. And that is impossible. And the complete discussion of invalidating these objections has preceded, and there is no benefit in repetition. • And here is the end of the deduced arguments from His being Exalted as Agent and Creator, and with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage presents a final argument and conclusion against an objection concerning divine agency. The objection is implicit: if an agent only acts at a time that is 'compatible' (al-muwāfiq) with its action, then the occurrence of that time and the changes associated with it would be independent of the agent's initiation. The author refutes this by showing that such a scenario implies that times and changes exist without being caused by the First Agent (al-fāʿil al-awwal), which is impossible (muḥāl). He then states that the full refutation of these questions has already been given earlier and there is no need to repeat it. Finally, he marks the end of the deduced proofs (al-wujūh al-mustanbiṭa) from God's being Agent (fāʿil) and Creator (mūjid), concluding with 'with Allah is success' (bi-llāh al-tawfīq). The argument emphasizes that every temporal event and change must be directly created by God; otherwise, one would admit an independent source of change, contradicting tawḥīd.

Definition of Qadir and Mujib: The Necessity of Divine Influence
Defines qadir and mujib, then proves God's influence is necessary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between a necessary agent (mujib) and a powerful agent (qadir), and why divine influence must be of the necessary type.

Core Idea
God's power is not a mere possibility; it necessitates the existence of effects.

This passage from al-Matalib al-‘Aliyah presents a key classification in Islamic cosmology: the difference between an agent that acts necessarily and one that can act or not. Understanding this distinction is crucial for appreciating the theological debate about divine causation and the eternity of the world. The author then argues that God's influence must be necessary, leading to a conclusion about the eternal existence of effects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Get a sense of the overall flow from definitions to proof.
The Arabic has some OCR issues (e.g., 'القحرة' should be 'القدرة'), but treat as given.
2
Identify the two definitions of qadir
Notice how the philosophers define qadir (as an efficient cause that knows its effect) and how another group divides efficient causes into mujib and qadir.
This classification is the foundation of the later argument.
3
Understand the classification of agents
The passage defines mujib as an agent that cannot not act, and qadir as one that can act or not. Then it defines qadir based on the ability to leave action.
This sets up the two possibilities for God's influence.
4
Follow the proof for God's necessity
Trace the argument: if God influenced necessarily, effects would be eternal; but contingent influence is impossible, so God's influence must be necessary.
The conclusion follows from the impossibility of the contingent option.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في الدلائل المستنبطة من صفة القحرة من الفعل عن
قالت الفلاسفة : القادر هو [ المؤثر (۱) ] الذي يكون عالماً بصدور أثره عنه (۲)] ومن الناس من قال : المؤثر إما أن يؤثر ، مع أنه يمتنع أن لا يؤثر . أو يؤثر [ مع (۳) ] أنه لا يمتنع أن لا يؤثر . والأول هو الموجب ، والثاني [هو (٤)] القادر. فعلى هذا : القادر هو الذي يكون متمكناً الترك ، ومن الترك بدلاً عن الفعل ، بحسب الدواعي المختلفة . إذا ثبت هذا ، فنقول : اتفق الكل على أنه لو كان تأثير الله [ تعالى (٥) ] في وجود الآثار على سبيل القسم الأول ، لزم دوام الآثار بدوامه . فنقول : إنه يمتنع أن يؤثر شيء في شيء على سبيل القسم الثاني ، وهو التأثير على سبيل الصحة ، فتعين أن يكون على سبيل القسم الأول ، وهو التأثير على سبيل الوجوب . وحينئذ يحصل المقصود
On the indications derived from the attribute of power (al-qudra) from action? The philosophers said: The powerful (al-qādir) is the efficient cause (al-mu'aththir) who knows the emanation of his effect from him. And among people there are those who said: The efficient cause either acts such that it is impossible for it not to act, or acts such that it is not impossible for it not to act. The first is the necessitating agent (al-mūjib), and the second is the powerful (al-qādir). On this basis: the powerful is the one who is able to leave (action), and to substitute leaving for acting, according to different motives. When this is established, we say: Everyone agrees that if the influence of God—exalted is He—upon the existence of effects were in the first way, then the effects would necessarily be eternal with His eternity. We say: It is impossible for something to influence something else in the second way, which is influence in the mode of possibility (ʿalā sabīl al-ṣiḥḥa), so it must be that it is in the first way, which is influence in the mode of necessity (ʿalā sabīl al-wujūb). And then the intended conclusion is obtained.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage begins with a brief title indicating it is on the indications derived from the attribute of power. It then presents two definitions of the powerful agent (al-qādir). First, the philosophers define it as an efficient cause (al-mu'aththir) that knows the emanation of its effect. Second, an alternative view divides efficient causes into two types: one that acts necessarily (cannot not act) and one that acts contingently (can not act). The first is called al-mūjib (necessitating agent), the second al-qādir (powerful agent). From this classification, a definition of al-qādir emerges: one who is able to abandon action and substitute non-action for action according to different motives. After establishing this, the author moves to a theological proof. It is agreed that if God's influence were of the first type (necessary), then the effects would be eternal with Him (since the cause is eternal). The author then argues that it is impossible for something to influence something else in the second, contingent way (influence in the mode of possibility). Therefore, God's influence must be in the first, necessary mode, leading to the conclusion that the effects are eternal. The argument proceeds step by step: definition, classification, agreement on consequence, impossibility of the alternative, and final determination.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That a 'necessary agent' (mujib) is compelled or lacks will.
Correction: In this context, 'necessary' means the effect necessarily follows from the agent's essence, not from external compulsion. It does not negate will or knowledge.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes the 'mujib' from the 'qadir'?
A) The mujib acts with knowledge, the qadir acts without knowledge.
B) The mujib acts necessarily (impossible not to act), while the qadir can act or not act.
C) The mujib acts only from habit, while the qadir acts from free choice.
D) The mujib's effect is temporal, while the qadir's effect is eternal.

Key Takeaway
The passage establishes that God's influence must be necessary, meaning that effects necessarily follow from His essence, leading to the conclusion that the effects are eternal.

?

?
The passage defines the powerful agent as one who can choose to act or not. But it concludes God’s influence is necessary, not contingent. Does that make you feel God is less free? Or does it assure you that His actions are perfectly consistent, unlike human whim? Examine your heart: do you want a God whose actions are predictable or unpredictable? Which gives you more peace?
?
If every effect of God is necessary, then your current state—your faith, your sins, your very breath—is a necessary consequence of His essence. How does that make you feel about your responsibility? Do you use the idea of God’s power as an excuse for complacency, or as a reason to urgently align your will with His necessary goodness?

First Proof Against Capability as Power to Act
Proof that the attribute of capability (qudra) in the sense of power to act at will is impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument against defining divine power as capability (tamakkun) to act or refrain at will.

Core Idea
Divine power cannot involve choice between acting and not acting, because that would require impossible temporal conditions.

This lesson examines the first argument from Islamic philosophical theology that refutes a particular understanding of God's power. The argument shows that if 'capability' means having the ability to either do or not do an act at a given time, logical contradictions follow. We'll walk through the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two possibilities
The proof starts by considering two possible interpretations of capability. Read the first part of the passage to identify them.
The first possibility is immediately deemed impossible.
2
Analyze the first possibility
See why the first possibility is impossible in itself: it would require simultaneous existence and non-existence of an act.
3
Analyze the second possibility
The second possibility involves capability to act in the future. The author uses a temporal condition to show it is false.
Power to act in the second time is conditioned by the presence of that time, which is impossible in the first time.
4
Examine the three temporal states
The author generalizes to three states: persistence, origination, and non-existence of the act. Each is proven false.
5
Conclude the impossibility
Since all possibilities and states lead to falsehood, the entire notion of capability in this sense is impossible.
The passage ends with 'wa Allah a'lam'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول ممتنع لعينه، لامتناع الاجتماع بين العدم وبين الوجود معاً، وإذا كان ممتنع الوجود، كانت القدرة عليه أولى بالامتناع والثاني أيضاً : باطل. لأن القدرة على إيقاع الفعل في الزمان الثاني، مشروط بحضور الزمان لكن حضور الزمان الثاني في الزمان عقلا، والموقوف على الممتنع : ممتنع . فيلزم أن يكون كون القادر قادراً على إيقاع الفعل في الزمان الثاني محالاً. ممتنعاً عقلاً، وما كان كذلك، امتنع كونه مقدوراً ، فثبت أن كون القادر قادراً على الفعل بمعنى كونه متمكناً من الفعل والترك، إما أن يثبت حال بقاء الفعل، أو حال حدوثه، أو حال عدمه . وثبت : أن الكل باطل فكان القول بإثبات القادر بهذا التفسير : محالاً والله أعلم
The first is impossible in itself, because of the impossibility of the conjunction of non-existence and existence together. And if it is impossible of existence, then power over it is more deserving of impossibility. And the second is also false, because power to perform the act in the second time is conditioned by the presence of that time, but the presence of the second time in the first time is impossible intellectually, and what depends on the impossible is impossible. So it necessarily follows that the being of the capable one as capable of performing the act in the second time is impossible, intellectually impossible. And whatever is like that, its being an object of power is impossible. So it is established that the being of the capable one as capable of the act in the sense of being able to do or not do, either it is established at the time of the persistence of the act, or at the time of its origination, or at the time of its non-existence. And it is established that all are false. So the statement affirming the capable one with this interpretation is impossible. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage presents a proof against the notion that God has power (qudra) in the sense of capability (tamakkun) to act or refrain from acting. The argument begins by considering two possibilities for such a capability: the first is immediately deemed impossible because it would require the simultaneous existence of a thing and its non-existence, which is logically contradictory. The second possibility is that the capable one has the ability to perform an act at a future time (the second time). The author argues that this is also false because power to perform an act in the second time is conditioned by the presence of that time. However, the presence of the second time in the first time is intellectually impossible—they are distinct temporal moments. Therefore, the dependence on an impossible condition renders the capability itself impossible. Consequently, it becomes impossible for the capable one to be capable of performing the act in the second time. The author then generalizes: the concept of being capable (in the sense of being able to do or not do) is examined under three states: at the time of the act's persistence, at its origination, or at its non-existence. In each of these, the capability is proven false, so the entire notion of capability in this sense is impossible. The passage ends with 'wa Allah a'lam' (God knows best).

Key Terms

قدرة
قادرية
تمكن
ممتنع
زمان
مقدور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's power includes the ability to arbitrarily choose to act at any future moment.
Correction: The proof shows that such capability would require the impossible presence of a future time in the present, making it rationally impossible.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, why is the second possibility (capability to act in the second time) false?
A) Because the second time does not exist at all.
B) Because power to act in the second time is conditioned by the presence of that time, but the second time cannot be present in the first time.
C) Because the capable one cannot have power over something that will exist later.
D) Because the second time is impossible in itself.

Key Takeaway
The concept of divine capability as power to act or refrain at will is rationally impossible because it leads to contradictions concerning time and existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Are you willing to accept that His responses are never delayed by any lack of capability, but are always perfectly timed according to His timeless will?
?
This proof shows that God's power is not a potential to act or refrain, but a necessary actuality. In your own life, do you sometimes treat God's power as if it were potential, waiting for conditions? How can you realign your heart to recognize His power as always already complete and active?

Impossibility of Eternal Capability
Argument against eternal capability (al-qudariyya al-azaliyya).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why capability (qudariyya) cannot be an eternal attribute, based on the contradiction between the act of creation and the nature of pre-eternity.

Core Idea
Eternal capability is impossible because it would require a temporal act in eternity.

This lesson examines the first branch of the second proof against capability as an attribute of God. The argument shows that if capability were eternal, it would involve bringing something from non-existence to existence, which implies being preceded by non-existence. But pre-eternity excludes any precedence. Hence eternal capability is contradictory.

Guided Path
1
Read the first part of the proof
Read the Arabic passage that argues against eternal capability. Notice how the author sets up the division.
2
Understand the definition of 'capable one'
The capable one is defined as one who can bring into existence. This definition is crucial for the argument.
3
Grasp the contradiction
The act of exiting non-existence to existence requires being preceded by non-existence, but pre-eternity negates being preceded. Recognize why this is impossible.
4
Follow the conclusion
The conclusion is that eternal capability is impossible because its object (the act) is impossible in itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية : لو كان القادر قادراً بهذا التفسير، لكانت هذه القادرية إما أن تكون ثابتة في الأزل، أو لا تكون . والقسمان باطلان . فبطل القول بثبوت القادرية. إنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع ثبوتها في الأزل، لأن القادر هو الذي يمكنه الإحداث والإخراج من العدم إلى الوجود، والقدرة على الشيء مشروطة بإمكان وجود ذلك المقدور في نفسه، لكن حقيقة الخروج من العدم إلى الوجود محال في الأزل، لأن هذه الحقيقة تقتضي المسبوقية بالغير، وحقيقة الأزل تنافي المسبوقية بالغير، والجمع بينهما محال . فيثبت : أن حصول الحدوث في الأزل : محال لعينه . وما كان محال لعينه، امتنع أن يكون مقدوراً، وإذا امتنع كونه مقدوراً، امتنع كون القادر قادراً عليه . فيثبت : أنه يمتنع ثبوت القادرية في الأزل. وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع أن تكون تلك القادرية صفة حادثة، لأنها لو كانت حادثة لافتقر إحداثها إلى تقدم قادرية أخرى، ولزم التسلسل . فيثبت : أنه لو حصلت القدرة بمعنى المكنة من الفعل والترك لكانت إما أن تكون أزلية، وإما أن تكون حادثة، وثبت فساد كل واحد من هذين القسمين، فكان ثبوت الملزوم : محالاً
The second proof: If the capable one were capable in this interpretation, then this capability (al-qudariyya) would either be established in pre-eternity (al-azal) or not. And both divisions are false. So the statement affirming capability is nullified. We said: It is impossible for it to be established in pre-eternity, because the capable one is one who can originate and bring forth from non-existence to existence, and power over a thing is conditioned by the possibility of the existence of that object of power in itself. But the reality of exiting from non-existence to existence is impossible in pre-eternity, because this reality necessitates being preceded by another, and the reality of pre-eternity negates being preceded by another, and combining them is impossible. So it is established that the occurrence of temporality (al-huduth) in pre-eternity is impossible in itself. And whatever is impossible in itself, it is impossible for it to be an object of power. And if it is impossible for it to be an object of power, it is impossible for the capable one to be capable of it. So it is established that it is impossible for capability to be established in pre-eternity. And we said: It is impossible for that capability to be a temporal attribute, because if it were temporal, its origination would depend on the precedence of another capability, and an infinite regress would follow. So it is established that if power in the sense of ability (al-makna) to act and refrain were to exist, it would either be pre-eternal or temporal, and the corruption of each of these two divisions is established, so the existence of the necessary implication (al-malzum) is impossible.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof against capability (al-qudariyya) in the sense of ability to act or refrain. The proof proceeds by division: such a capability, if it existed, would have to be either pre-eternal (azaliyya) or temporal (haditha). Both alternatives are shown to be false. First, pre-eternal capability is impossible because the capable one is defined as one who can bring something from non-existence to existence. However, the reality of 'exiting from non-existence to existence' necessarily implies being preceded by something (the state of non-existence), which is a form of being preceded by another. Pre-eternity (al-azal) is defined as that which has no beginning and cannot be preceded by another. Therefore, the combination of 'exiting from non-existence' and 'pre-eternity' is impossible, because they are contradictory. Hence, the occurrence of a temporal act (huduth) in pre-eternity is impossible in itself. What is impossible in itself cannot be an object of power, so the capable one cannot be capable of it. Consequently, pre-eternal capability is impossible. Second, temporal capability is also impossible because if it were a temporal attribute, its own origination would require a prior capability to bring it into existence, and that prior capability would itself need a cause, leading to an infinite regress (tasalsul), which is absurd. Since both alternatives are false, the very concept of capability (al-qudariyya) in this sense cannot hold; thus, the claim that God has such a capability is invalid.

قادرية
أزل
حدوث
مقدور
مسبوقية بالغير
إحداث

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God's power can be an eternal attribute that is actualized only when He wills.
Correction: The proof argues that the very concept of 'ability to create' involves a temporal dimension that cannot be reconciled with an eternal attribute, because the act of creation implies a beginning.

Checkpoint
Why does the author claim that eternal capability is impossible?
A) Because God cannot have any attributes in pre-eternity.
B) Because the act of exiting from non-existence to existence requires being preceded by non-existence, which contradicts the nature of pre-eternity.
C) Because pre-eternal attributes cannot be the subject of power.
D) Because pre-eternity is a temporal concept.

Key Takeaway
Eternal capability is impossible because the act of creation implies a beginning, which contradicts the nature of pre-eternity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson proves that the very concept of 'coming from non-existence' requires a beginning. You yourself were brought from non-existence into existence by God. Have you ever truly paused to realize that before you existed, you were nothing? How does that reality change the way you live today? Will you carry that awareness into your next prayer?
?
If God's power to create is not an eternal attribute in the way you might have imagined, what does that tell you about the intimate, moment-by-moment nature of your dependence on Him? Are you living as if your existence is self-sufficient, or do you feel the weight of every breath being a new act of creation?
?
The author argues that what is impossible in itself cannot be an object of power. Are there things in your life that you treat as 'possible' for God to fix while you refuse to acknowledge their actual impossibility? Is your faith in God's power truly anchored in what He has revealed, or in your own imagination?

Impossibility of Temporal Capability and Infinite Regress
Argument against temporal capability (al-qudariyya al-haditha) and infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why capability (qudariyya) cannot be a temporal attribute and how this leads to an infinite regress.

Core Idea
Temporal capability leads to an infinite regress of causes.

This lesson examines the second branch of the proof: that capability cannot be temporal. The argument demonstrates that if capability were a created attribute, its own creation would require a prior capability, leading to an infinite chain. Since that is impossible, temporal capability is also false.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the proof
Read the Arabic passage that argues against temporal capability. Notice the conditional statement.
2
Understand the dependency
If capability is temporal, its origination depends on a prior capability. Grasp why this is necessary.
3
See the infinite regress
The prior capability would itself require a cause, leading to an endless chain. Recognize why this is absurd.
4
Conclude the overall proof
The passage concludes that both branches (eternal and temporal) are false, so the concept of capability as defined is impossible.

Source Text

Objection and First Refutation: The Condition of Ability
Objection and first refutation concerning the condition of ability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that pre-eternity itself acts as a hindrance to God's act and the first refutation showing that ability to act requires the act to be possible in itself.

Core Idea
Pre-eternity cannot hinder because ability requires possibility of the act.

The author has argued that God's act is temporal. The objector proposes that pre-eternity itself could serve as a hindrance, allowing God to be powerful yet inactive. The author first notes that this objection also undermines the position of essential causality, then provides a direct refutation based on the nature of ability.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the opening lines where the objector suggests that pre-eternity (al-azal) acts as a hindrance to origination. Notice the reasoning: it is intellectually conceivable for a capable being to be hindered.
The objector does not deny God's power, but claims it is blocked.
2
Understand the side note about ta'thir dhati
The author points out that this objection also applies to those who affirm essential causality (al-ta'thir al-dhati), because it would force them to say God was effecting in pre-eternity, leading to tahsil al-hasil (attaining the already attained), which is impossible.
This shows the objection is not unique to the author's position.
3
Study the first refutation
Read the author's answer: ability (al-makna) to act or refrain cannot exist unless the act itself is possible. Since an act in pre-eternity is impossible (as shown earlier), the ability cannot exist.
This is a direct refutation based on the definition of ability.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this refutation preserves the temporality of creation. If ability requires possibility, and pre-eternal act is impossible, then there is no ability in pre-eternity, so no hindrance is needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : إنه تعالى في الأزل كان موصوفاً بالقدرة على الإيجاد، إلا أن قيام الأزل يجري مجرى المانع من الإيجاد، ولا يمتنع في العقل أن يكون القادر قادراً على الفعل إلا أنه يتعذر عليه الفعل لمانع . ثم نقول : هذا أيضاً لازم على القائلين بالتأثير الذاتي، لأنه يلزم كونه مؤثراً في وجود العالم في الأزل، أن العالم كان موجوداً في الأزل، وذلك يقتضي تحصيل الحاصل، وهو محال والجواب عن الأول : أن نقول : المكنة من الفعل والترك يمتنع حصولها، إلا حيث كان حصول الفعل ممكناً في نفسه، فلما كان حصول الفعل في الأزل ممتنعاً، امتنع كون القادر قادراً عليه . بقي أن يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : القادرية كانت حاصلة في الأزل، إلا أنه تعذر الفعل لمانع ؟ فنقول : هذا باطل .. ويدل عليه وجوه : الأول : إنه لما كانت المكنة حاصلة في الأزل، فتعذر الفعل يمتنع يكون لعدم المقتضى، بل لا بد وأن يكون لوجود المانع وعلى هذا التقدير يكون المانع من الإيجاد : أزلياً. وعندكم : أن الأزلي يمتنع زواله، فيلزم امتناع زوال ذلك المانع . ولو كان الأمر كذلك، لما زال الامتناع فقط الثاني : إنه لو حصل مانع يمنع من حصول ذلك الأثر . فإما أن يكون ذلك المانع . بحيث يزول أو لا يزول. فإن زال، كان زواله مختصاً بوقت معين . لأن كل ما كان موجوداً، ثم صار معدوماً . فإن لابد
For it may be said: Why is it not permissible to say that He, exalted, in pre-eternity was described with power to originate, except that the state of pre-eternity acts as a hindrance to origination, and it is not impossible intellectually that the capable one be capable of the act but the act is difficult for him due to a hindrance. Then we say: This also follows necessarily for those who affirm essential causality (al-ta'thir al-dhati), because it would necessitate that He is an effecter in the existence of the world in pre-eternity, [and] that the world existed in pre-eternity, and that requires attainment of what is already attained (tahsil al-hasil), which is impossible. The answer to the first [part of the objection] is that we say: The ability (al-makna) to act and refrain cannot exist except where the occurrence of the act is possible in itself. Since the occurrence of the act in pre-eternity is impossible, it is impossible for the capable one to be capable of it. It remains to be said: Why is it not permissible to say that capability (al-qudariyya) existed in pre-eternity, but the act was prevented by a hindrance? We say: This is false. And there are proofs for it: First: Since the ability existed in pre-eternity, the prevention of the act cannot be due to absence of the requisite, but rather must be due to existence of a hindrance. On this assumption, the hindrance to origination is pre-eternal. And according to you [the opponents], the pre-eternal cannot cease, so the cessation of that hindrance is impossible. If that were the case, the impossibility would never cease. Second: If there were a hindrance that prevents the attainment of that effect, then that hindrance either ceases or does not cease. If it ceases, its cessation is specific to a particular time, because everything that exists and then becomes non-existent... indeed it must... [incomplete]
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage presents an objection against the previous proofs and the author's response. The objector suggests that it is possible to say that God in pre-eternity possessed the power to create, but the very state of pre-eternity itself acted as a hindrance preventing the act. This would mean that God was capable but unable to act due to a hindrance, which is intellectually conceivable. The author then notes that this objection also applies to those who affirm essential causality (al-ta'thir al-dhati), as they would be forced to claim that God was an effecter in pre-eternity, leading to the world being pre-eternal, which is absurd (tahsil al-hasil). The author then gives two answers. First, the ability (al-makna) to act or refrain requires that the act itself be possible in itself. Since the occurrence of an act in pre-eternity is impossible (as shown earlier), the capable one cannot be capable of it. Then the objector persists: why not say capability existed in pre-eternity but was prevented by a hindrance? The author asserts this is false and provides two proofs. The first proof: if ability existed in pre-eternity, the prevention must be due to an external hindrance, not absence of the requisite. That hindrance would then be pre-eternal. But the opponents hold that the pre-eternal cannot cease; thus the hindrance would never cease, and the impossibility would never end. The second proof (incomplete): if a hindrance exists, it either ceases or does not. If it ceases, its cessation occurs at a specific time, implying change in the eternal, which leads to further difficulties. The text ends abruptly.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God could be powerful in pre-eternity but unable to act due to a hindrance.
Correction: The author argues that if the act is impossible in itself, there is no ability. Pre-eternity makes the act impossible because it would require a change in the eternal, so ability cannot exist.

C) The capable one must be willing to act.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you wait for God's help in a difficult situation, do you truly believe that His delay is not due to a 'hindrance' but because the act wasn't yet possible in His wisdom? How can you actively remind yourself of this truth when impatience arises?
?

?
If ability requires possibility, then God's power is not arbitrary but deeply connected to the nature of reality. How does this change the way you view your own struggles—are you asking God for things that are truly possible according to His wisdom? What would it mean for you to submit to His definition of possibility today?

Persistence of the Objection and Two Proofs Against a Pre-Eternal Hindrance
Two proofs against the claim of a pre-eternal hindrance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the opponent's persistence and the two proofs demonstrating that a pre-eternal hindrance is impossible.

Core Idea
A pre-eternal hindrance would be eternal and irremovable, making the cessation of impossibility impossible.

After the first refutation, the objector persists: why not say capability (al-qudariyya) existed in pre-eternity but was prevented by a hindrance? The author declares this false and provides two proofs. The first proof shows that such a hindrance would be pre-eternal and thus never removable. The second proof (though incomplete) argues that the hindrance either ceases or not, each leading to contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's persistence
The objector now asks: 'Why not say the capability existed in pre-eternity, but the act was prevented by a hindrance?' This is a refined version of the earlier objection.
The objector accepts that ability requires possibility, but now claims capability (qudariyya) is different.
2
Study the first proof
Read the first proof: if capability existed, the prevention must be due to an external hindrance, not absence of requisite. That hindrance would be pre-eternal. Since the opponents hold that the pre-eternal cannot cease, the hindrance would never cease, so the impossibility of creation would never end.
This proof uses the opponent's own principle against them.
3
Examine the second proof (incomplete)
The second proof begins: if a hindrance exists, it either ceases or does not. If it ceases, its cessation is specific to a time, implying change in the eternal. The text ends abruptly, but the argument suggests a temporal hindrance requires a cause for its cessation, leading to infinite regress.
The OCR is incomplete; the argument continues beyond this chunk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : إنه تعالى في الأزل كان موصوفاً بالقدرة على الإيجاد، إلا أن قيام الأزل يجري مجرى المانع من الإيجاد، ولا يمتنع في العقل أن يكون القادر قادراً على الفعل إلا أنه يتعذر عليه الفعل لمانع . ثم نقول : هذا أيضاً لازم على القائلين بالتأثير الذاتي، لأنه يلزم كونه مؤثراً في وجود العالم في الأزل، أن العالم كان موجوداً في الأزل، وذلك يقتضي تحصيل الحاصل، وهو محال والجواب عن الأول : أن نقول : المكنة من الفعل والترك يمتنع حصولها، إلا حيث كان حصول الفعل ممكناً في نفسه، فلما كان حصول الفعل في الأزل ممتنعاً، امتنع كون القادر قادراً عليه . بقي أن يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : القادرية كانت حاصلة في الأزل، إلا أنه تعذر الفعل لمانع ؟ فنقول : هذا باطل .. ويدل عليه وجوه : الأول : إنه لما كانت المكنة حاصلة في الأزل، فتعذر الفعل يمتنع يكون لعدم المقتضى، بل لا بد وأن يكون لوجود المانع وعلى هذا التقدير يكون المانع من الإيجاد : أزلياً. وعندكم : أن الأزلي يمتنع زواله، فيلزم امتناع زوال ذلك المانع . ولو كان الأمر كذلك، لما زال الامتناع فقط الثاني : إنه لو حصل مانع يمنع من حصول ذلك الأثر . فإما أن يكون ذلك المانع . بحيث يزول أو لا يزول. فإن زال، كان زواله مختصاً بوقت معين . لأن كل ما كان موجوداً، ثم صار معدوماً . فإن لابد
For it may be said: Why is it not permissible to say that He, exalted, in pre-eternity was described with power to originate, except that the state of pre-eternity acts as a hindrance to origination, and it is not impossible intellectually that the capable one be capable of the act but the act is difficult for him due to a hindrance. Then we say: This also follows necessarily for those who affirm essential causality (al-ta'thir al-dhati), because it would necessitate that He is an effecter in the existence of the world in pre-eternity, [and] that the world existed in pre-eternity, and that requires attainment of what is already attained (tahsil al-hasil), which is impossible. The answer to the first [part of the objection] is that we say: The ability (al-makna) to act and refrain cannot exist except where the occurrence of the act is possible in itself. Since the occurrence of the act in pre-eternity is impossible, it is impossible for the capable one to be capable of it. It remains to be said: Why is it not permissible to say that capability (al-qudariyya) existed in pre-eternity, but the act was prevented by a hindrance? We say: This is false. And there are proofs for it: First: Since the ability existed in pre-eternity, the prevention of the act cannot be due to absence of the requisite, but rather must be due to existence of a hindrance. On this assumption, the hindrance to origination is pre-eternal. And according to you [the opponents], the pre-eternal cannot cease, so the cessation of that hindrance is impossible. If that were the case, the impossibility would never cease. Second: If there were a hindrance that prevents the attainment of that effect, then that hindrance either ceases or does not cease. If it ceases, its cessation is specific to a particular time, because everything that exists and then becomes non-existent... indeed it must... [incomplete]
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage presents an objection against the previous proofs and the author's response. The objector suggests that it is possible to say that God in pre-eternity possessed the power to create, but the very state of pre-eternity itself acted as a hindrance preventing the act. This would mean that God was capable but unable to act due to a hindrance, which is intellectually conceivable. The author then notes that this objection also applies to those who affirm essential causality (al-ta'thir al-dhati), as they would be forced to claim that God was an effecter in pre-eternity, leading to the world being pre-eternal, which is absurd (tahsil al-hasil). The author then gives two answers. First, the ability (al-makna) to act or refrain requires that the act itself be possible in itself. Since the occurrence of an act in pre-eternity is impossible (as shown earlier), the capable one cannot be capable of it. Then the objector persists: why not say capability existed in pre-eternity but was prevented by a hindrance? The author asserts this is false and provides two proofs. The first proof: if ability existed in pre-eternity, the prevention must be due to an external hindrance, not absence of the requisite. That hindrance would then be pre-eternal. But the opponents hold that the pre-eternal cannot cease; thus the hindrance would never cease, and the impossibility would never end. The second proof (incomplete): if a hindrance exists, it either ceases or does not. If it ceases, its cessation occurs at a specific time, implying change in the eternal, which leads to further difficulties. The text ends abruptly.
